NEMORANDUM FOR THE RECORD

SURJECT: Compromise of Cover:

As

a result of information obtained from

reliable sources who served in Vietnam, it has

been established that the above named individual

should be presumed to have been compromised as

a CIA employee to the North Victnamese Intclligence

Service us

of

January 1968. It is presuned that

• the identification of this individual as a CIA

employee was passed by the North Vietnamese to the

Soviets.

Department ci State

Washington, D.C. 20520

Dear Mr. Secretary:

It is with regret that I find it necessarv to

submit my resignation

to be effective November 23, 1974.

My dusies with the Department of State have been

source of

great interest and

pleasure to me, and

I look forward to the possibility of further service

with the Department should circumstances permit my

consideration for employment in the future.

Sincercly,

David E. Murphy

3. BY REVIEWING OFFICIAL

CONMENTS OP DEVIANIMO ORPICIAL

Under Mr. Murphy's leadership the Paris Station became very opera-

tionally oriented, concentrating on high priority targets, and much

exceptionally fine intelligence and counterintelligence production resulted.

I have some doubt that these operational successes - as. outstanding as they

were - rcally required the total number of personnel of all categories who

wire

committed to them.

Nevertheless, Mr. Murphy made Paris a shining

example for all other large stations.

OVERALL RATING: OUTSTANDING

1.

At the end of May 1971, Mr. Murphy will leave

He distinguished himself by having

molded this Station into a cohesive, well-disciplined,

of Mr. Murphy as, overall, the

most effective chief of

a major station

in the European

Division.

His earlict

fitness reports and his excellent record

attest to this.

in Paris

2.

the Paris Station has continued to make significant

progress on all major fronts.

As examples, l can cite

two direct soviet recruitment attempts, an imaginative

effort to get closer to several other primary Sovict

targets, a perceptible improvement in

our French liaison

relationships,

a marked increase in both

quality

and

quantity of priority ccononic intelligence reporting,

the acquisition of

new sources to

cover the french

internal

scene,

and a revitalization of several cxisting

assets into producers of valuable intelligence.

Mr. Murphy's case he personally becones

involved in each

period. He has excellent judgement, a quick mind and a thorough knowledge of

:Outstanding

1.

Long before il. Murphy departed for Paris in June

1968, he began preparing himself for this assignment as Chief

of Station by reading files, interviewing personnel, and

discussing

cases.

Is a result, on arrival in Paris

he was

already well oriented concerning the Station's problems and

had formulated plans

for revitalizing it.

2.

The entire year in Paris has of course been over-

shadowed by the Vietnam Peace Conference and a large proportion

of the Station's effort has perforce been devoted to supporting

the U.S. delegation.

The Station has responded exceptionally

well to this demand

though it has forced a slow-down in normal

Station activities.

A number of other events have also taken place in

or concerniny france which have forced the Station

the past nine months to perform firemen's duty -- the

May-June riots which extended into August, the dissolution

of the Assenhly and re-election of deputies, the Croch crisis

beginnins 21 sugust, tre December monotary crisis,

the Near

Fast crisis, continued student unrest, the President's trip

and currently the problems precipitated by Debaulle's resig-

All of these developments have been covered

1.

while the exceptional events enumeraled above have

forced

the Station 10

eilorts on the innediate

issues, Mr. Surphy

nonetholess proceeded with the lonker

range coals at the

spation.

He has

worked at improving ic-

1ad10ns with the Fronin

services, personally becoming deeply

involved even in routine liaison

activity.

Consequently,

our relations duriny the past nine nonths with the French

have improved considerably.

This improvement can partially

be attributed to a reawakening on the part of the French

Government to the Communist and sen Left threat (which was

brought into focus by the blay-June riots) but it was also

in large measure due to sir. Murphy's concerted efiorts to

cultivate selected officials, initiate substantive dis-

cussions and increase our own level of exchange with the

Services.

Operations against the Communist Party have been re-

activated with emphasis on the international aspects of the

Party, particularly support of subversion abroad.

Operations

against the large Soviet and Chinese targets are

beginning

to move ahead. Production-wise, the take fron both

increased significantly during 1968. Ne

expect further increase in 1969.

There are still many weak spots

in the Paris Station

and many refinements

and adjustments

Murphy has made an exceptional beginning; the Station ls

1 April 1965

MEMORANDUM IN LIEU OF ANNUAL FITNESS REPORT

(For the period ending 31

March 1965)

SUBJECT: Mr. David E. Murphy

1. This report is the first full year report of Mr. Murphy's

performance as Chief of the SR Division.

2. Perhaps his greatest contribution during this past year has

been the energizing of the Division's several components with a

congequent very noticeable increase in the rfforts of the Clandestine

Services as a whole against our Soviet targets. Mr. Murphy's

enthusiasm and imagination have been contagious, and we are ag

a result profiting from his sound approach to the role and mission

of his Division.

He has fully understood tie fact that the SR Division

cannot alone discharge the responsibilities of the Clandestine Services

for intelligence and counter-intelligence activity against our Soviet

requirements, but must harness the interest and the energies of all

the area divisions. In this respect, Mr. Murphy is achicving nothing

short of remarkable success. His arrangements with DODS are also

improving the quality of that Division's work in the SR field, while

his general administration of his Division from a managerial point of

view has continued to be excellent.

3. The overall evaluation of Mr. Murphy's performance during

this past year, including his regard for cost and manpower factorg,

is outstanding. It is because of the quality of this performance that

favorable consideration has been given in principle to the gradual

investment of an increasing portion of the inanpower assets of the

Clandestine Services to his Division. His plans and his accomplish-

inents to date justify confidence that these increases are being well

invegied and will provide a maximum return,

Thomas H. Karamessines

Asgistant Deputy Director for Plang

1 April 1964

MEMORANDUM IN LIEU OF ANNUAL FITNESS REPORT

(For the period ending 31 March 1964)

SUBJECT: Mr. David E. Murphy

Mr. Murphy relinquished his duties as Chich, Eastern

Europe Division in September 1963 and took over his present respon-

sibilltiea as Chief of the SR Division at that time. This report coverg

the period from 1 April 1963 to the present and thua includes comments

on his performance as Chief, EE Division and Chief, SR Division.

2. Mr. Murphy combines an extraordinary talent for this work

with a considerable and varied experience in it. His previous report

indicated that he wag turning in an outstandirig performance in dealing

with the affairs of the EF. Division, and he continued this level of his

performance in the first six months covered by this report. A general

reorganization of sentor officers in the Clandestine Services offered

the opportunity to put Mr. Murphy in charge of the division which he

had long aspired to direct and for which position he was eminently

qualified, both linguistically and by field expericace. He is showing

excellent results in refurbishing the Diviaion and giving it new life

and impetus.

His considerable energies enable him to give an out-

standing performance in managing and directing his Division's affairs

while at the same time engaging personally and most actively in a

number of very important Divisional caseg.

His competence includes

awareness of the need for keeping his costs down and getting the

taximum from his manpower.

He is showing imagination and

initiative and is probably the best qualified and best prepared officer

ever to head the Division,

Thomas

Karameggines

Assintant Deputy Director for Plans

Reviewing Official:

Richard Helme

Deputy Director for Plane

I have noted the above report.

1E Muple

David E. Murphy

18 April 1903

NE MORANDUM FOR: Director of Personnel

SUBJECT:

Fitness Report - Mr. David E. Murphy

1. This memorandum is in lieu of the Fitness Report Form

on Mr. Murphy and covere the period from 1 April 1962 through

31 March 1963, during which Mr. Murphy hag nerved as Chief

of the Eastern Europe Division.

After a long series of asgignments datire feuen April 1948

aid involving duty at Tokyo,

Karlarube ard Berlin where

he served as Chief of Base of that important installation, Mr.

Murphy returned to Headquarters in August 1901 as Depuly Chief

os the EE Division and became Chief of that Division in June 1962.

I should like to quote fron the fitnesa report on Mr. Murphy written

as the time he was assuming his new respondibilities as Chief of

EE Division: "There in every reason to believe that dar. Murphy

will manage the EE Division in the same outstanding ander with

which he won the ungrudging respect of the berlin corrunity as

the leader of American Intelligence in that area." A previous

tess report covering hig firat year as Chief of Base, Berlin

is equally laudatory.

3. In his responsibility for streamlining and improving the

ellectiveness of his Divinion in both its headquarters ard overseas.

postures, Mr. Mürphy his been energetic and imiginalive. Heig

an authority on the situation in West Germany but carticularly in

Berlin and has played a highly useful role in government councile

on these problems. He has excellent working knowledge of Russian,

French and German, and his operational experience as a result

4. In conducting the affaire of his Division during this

past year, Mr. Murphy has without question borne out the

prediction that he would turn in an outstanding performance.

He has done this and continues to do it.

Thomas H. Karamessines

The only weaknesses I have noted f

he is never unreasonable nor in any sense dictatorial, and he has demon-

strated the capnelty of quickly developing. and rotalnine the full

loyalty, cooperation and respect of the officers with whom he works.

It 1s, I think, signiflcant also that the respect, which other officers

hold for Subject Increases in direct proportion in the level of pro-

fessional competence and experience whlch these officers attain.

In assessing Subject's pertormance and capabilitles, it should be

pointed out that he has been officially recommended for promotion

from grade G5-15 to grade G3-16 and

that he has been officially recom-

mended to succeed the present incumbent as Chief of Base, B0B. Further

comments concerning subject in this connection are contained in

EGBT- 100j dated 28 September 1958, the covering dispatch to this

Pitness Report, which should be read in conjunetlon therenlth.

SUBJECT

Service In the Clandostine Services

Records Comnittee

I wish to take this opportunity to thank you

for your scivice as a monber ol the CS Records Committee.

The contributions which you have made to our deliberations

have been of considerable assistance to me and to the cs

records progiam..

I believe that effective records and

systems are vital to the success of an intelligence organi

zatlon and that the Records Committee plays an extremely

Important role in ensuring that these systems are consonant

with more pressing and dianatic opcrational and policy

requirements.

The advice,

aysistance and participation

of yourself and other senior officials have enabled us

to mect our obligations and

make steady improvement in

this area.

I hopo I may continue

to count on your

tions, initiative and advice in this area in the future.

TO Raans

Thomas H. Karamessines

Mr. Willla Harvey

APO 742, US Forcon

1. As the Commanding Officer of this unit, it gives mo particular

pleanure 1o extond my appreciation to Mr. David Murphy and Mr.

Llebonau for the able and extremoly valuable asgislance which they

rendered to an oporation of this unit on 24 May 1959.

2. Mr. Murphy, when informed on Sunday 21 May that norse

ianistance was noeded by this unlt, despite the short notice, whole-

heartedly and unstintingly rendered advice and logistical support.

Because of unforescon circumstances, cortain support was lacking

for a particular operation,

and Mr. Murphy immediately proferred

the necessary aid. In discussing the various phases of the operation,

Mr. Murphy was good enough to share his rich experience with repre-

sentatives of this unit and thus faciliate implementation of the project.

3. Mr. Ilebenau's consideration, tact and'concern over the

security. and success of the operation merit praise.

Despite the ahort

timo allocated to Mr. Liebenau's phase in the operation, he consistently

deferred to the wishes of the members of this unit, recognizing diat

security of the operation was paramount.

4. Such cooperation and apirit of friendliness as exhibitod both

by Mr. Murphy and Mr. Liebenau are a

very welcome new page in the

relationship between this unit and your organization. It id a significant

stop toward the lype of coordination and cooperation wich will in the

last analysis benefit the intelligence community to the decriment of the

opposition.

ce: Mr. Gaines
